тАШрдкреНрд░ рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдиреАрдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрдпреГрдЪрдореЗрдХрд╛рджрд╢рдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рджрд┐рд╡реЛрджрд╛рд╕рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рддрд░реНрджрдирд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд░рд╛рдЬрд░реНрд╖реЗрд░рд┐рджрдВ рддреНрд░реИрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдВ рдкрд╡рдорд╛рдирд╕реЛрдорджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рдХрдореН ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рдореНрдпрддреЗ-тАЩ рдкреНрд░ рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдиреАрд╢реНрдЪрддреБрд░реНрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддрд┐рд░реНрджреИрд╡реЛрджрд╛рд╕рд┐рдГ рдкреНрд░рддрд░реНрджрдирдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЧрддрдГ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧрдГ рее

Jamison Brereton

96 (808)
Soma Pavama╠Дna
Pratardana Daivod─Бsi
24 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
This twenty-four-verse hymn, immediately following three five-verse hymns in the same meter, can easily be made to fit the sequence if it is analyzed as consisting of a collection of four-verse hymns, as Oldenberg clearly states (1888: 201). The six hymns thus obtained show different degrees of internal cohesion.
For example, the first four verses display clear thematic unity and development. The first verse is explicitly martial, with Soma as a warrior about to charge, a pic ture continued in the following verse. In verse 3 he achieves one of the most desired results of Vedic warfare, wide space for us to inhabit, and with this obtained, verse 4 articulates a counter-message, that of peace and nonviolence. Indra is explicitly mentioned in the first three verses, and comradeship is a central theme, as is seen in verses 1, 2, and 4.
The second hymn (vss. 5тАУ8) shows stylistic progression. It begins with a rhe torically restricted verse (5), consisting primarily of seven repetitions of the word тАЬbegetterтАЭ with different genitive complements. The next verse (6) continues the dominantly nominal construction of vs. 5, but with a more varied verbal repertoire, though the nominative-genitive syntagm persists. Verse 7 continues to describe the qualities and characteristic actions of Soma, in the 3rd person, though it abandons the strict nominal style. And finally vs. 8 breaks out into the dynamic 2nd person and imperative mood.
The third group (vss. 9тАУ12) ends with a characteristic hymn-final summary verse, which seems to mark a decisive break from what follows. Although no clear the matic unity imposes itself on the four verses, the focus on SomaтАЩs relationship with our ancestral ritualists and our hope that this relationship will continue fruitfully is noticeable, especially in the last two verses (11тАУ12). On the other hand, it is difficult to identify any unifying features in the next group of four (vss. 13тАУ16), which con sist primarily of standard soma-hymn tropes. In verses 17тАУ20 Soma as poet (esp. in vss. 17тАУ18) and his journey from the filter to the cups provide a weak cohesion. In the final group (vss. 21тАУ24), three verses (22тАУ24) contain courtship imagery, and the root krand тАЬroarтАЭ is prominent.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the structure of this hymn, see published introduction. Although the larger structure involves a series of independent four-vs. hymns, there are a number of echoes across these hymns, noted below, that may have influenced their being grouped together

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe leader of the host, a hero, advances in front of the chariots intent on seizing the cattle (of the enemy); his army exults; making their oblations to Indra prosperous for the friendly (worshippers), Soma assumes the hastily made robes (of curds and milk).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Hastily made: rabhas─Бni = indrasya vegen─Бgame nimitt─Бni,?caused by Indra’s hasty arrival

Jamison Brereton

The army-leader, the champion, at the forefront of the chariots, goes forth seeking cattle. His army bristles with excitement. Making the invocations of Indra beneficial for his comrades, Soma puts on his ravishing garments.

Griffith

IN forefront of the cars forth goes the Hero, the Leader, winning spoil: his host rejoices.
Soma endues his robes of lasting colours, and blesses, for his friends, their calls on Indra.

Geldner

Als tapferer Heerf├╝hrer zieht er K├╝he begehrend aus an der Spitze der Wagen. Kampffroh ist sein Heer. Die Indraanrufungen macht er f├╝r die Freunde gl├╝ckbringend; Soma legt seine grellen Gew├дnder an.

Grassmann

Voran den Wagen geht des Heeres F├╝hrer, der Held voll Kampflust und es freut sein Heer sich; Den Freunden segnend ihren Indra-Anruf legt Soma an die gl├дnzenden Gew├дnder.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe priests express his green-tinted (juice); he mounts the chariot unyoked by the horse-driving salutations; the wise Soma the friend of Indra goes to meet the worshipper.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The tawny ones [=fingers] jointly groom his tawny (horse), without resting, with acts of reverence that spur on the horse.
The comrade of Indra mounts the chariot; the knowing one drives with him to our good thought.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The published translation doesnтАЩt make it sufficiently clear that тАЬwithout restingтАЭ qualifies the тАЬtawny (horse).тАЭ Geldner and Renou construe gen. ├нndrasya with the chariot, while I take it with the comrade - and Ober vacillates (comrade II.100, chariot II.204). Since ├нndrasya is positioned between chariot and comrade, word order doesnтАЩt help. In my view тАШcomradeтАЩ is inherently relational and generally needs to be defined with reference to another being or beings, as comrade to someone, hence my tr. See also nearby

Griffith

Men decked with gold adorn his golden tendril, incessantly with steed-impelling homage.
The Friend of Indra mounts his car well-knowing, he comes thereon to meet the prayer we offer.

Geldner

Die goldenen Finger putzen sein goldfarbiges Ro├Я unabl├дssig unter Verbeugungen, die das Ro├Я zur Eile treiben. Als Freund besteigt er Indra┬┤s Wagen. Durch ihn gelangt der Wissende zur Gunst des Gottes.

Grassmann

Die goldnen Finger streicheln seinen Goldhengst mit Ehrfurcht ihn, den keine Treiber spornen; Als Indra’s Freund besteigt er seinen Wagen und kommt dadurch in seine Gunst, der Kluge.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDivine Soma, who are the beverage of Indra, flow at our sacrifice for (his) abundant food; sending water, causing rain to fall upon heaven and upon this earth, (come) from the wide (firmament, and) being purified bestow upon us wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Purify yourself, o god, for the conclave of gods, for great delight, o Soma, as IndraтАЩs drink.
Creating the waters and making this heaven rain, from the wide (realm) make wide space for us as you are being purified.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The phrase dy─Б╠Бm ut├йm─Б╠Бm raises a number of questions. First, what is ut├б conjoining? Although it is tempting to suggest тАЬheaven and this (earth),тАЭ this would produce the pragmatically unlikely тАЬcausing тАж this (earth) to rain.тАЭ Moreover, there are numerous exx. of prthiv ╠е ─л╠Бс╣Г dy─Б╠Бm ut├йm─Б╠Бm тАЬearth and this heavenтАЭ (III.32.8, 34.8, X.88.3, 9, 121.1). It seems that the last part of that phrase, containing only the second NP, has been extracted from the fuller expression and inserted here, with the ut├б pleonastic+++(=redundant)+++, or loosely conjoining the participial phrases kс╣Ыс╣Зv├бnn ap├бс╕е and varс╣г├бyan dy─Б╠Бm ut├йm─Б╠Бm despite its position within the NP. On the clash between the near deictic ay├бm тАШthis hereтАЩ and heaven, which is generally qualified by the distal deictic asa├║ тАШthat yonderтАЩ, see disc. ad VIII.40.4 - also for the fem. gender that dy─Б╠Бm must show here.

Geldner tr. d as implicitly comparative, тАЬmach uns die Bahn noch breiter als breit,тАЭ presumably because of the abl. ur├│с╕е. But ─Б╠Бwith preceding abl. almost always expresses the source and is not used with a comparative. The few passages, grouped in GrassmannтАЩs 7) тАЬvor andern, d.h. in h├╢herm vorzuglichern Grade als andereтАЭ (p. 169), that do show something like that sense (several in that category are best interpr.

otherwise) depend on ─Б╠Бv├бram тАЬthe choice from among тАжтАЭ Moreover, varivasy├бdoes not have a comparative sense тАШmake wider spaceтАЩ but merely тАШmake wide spaceтАЩ. In our passage the point seems to be that Soma is already positioned in a wide place, from which he can act to provide us with the same.

English translation:

тАЬFlow for our immunity from defeat and slaughter, flow for our welfare, for the great sacrifice for all the gods; all these my friends desire this; this I desire, O Soma Pavam─Бna.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For freedom from overthrow and freedom from assault purify yourself, for well-being, for lofty wholeness.
This do all these comrades desire; this do I desire, o self-purifying
Soma.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Oldenberg points out, bс╣Ыhat├й is a masc./neut. form apparently modifying two (or at least one) fem. nouns, svast├бye sarv├бt─Бtaye. Renou takes it as a third term: тАЬpour тАж le haut (rang),тАЭ but in his n. he acknowledges the Oldenberg/Geldner acceptance of gender mismatch here, noting also that that interpr. produces two pairs of paired datives, the negated violence words in p─Бda a and the positive -ti-abstracts in b. In my view pattern may trump gender here. ItтАЩs also worth noting that the cadence produced by bс╣Ыhat├й is bad, and it would be fixed by a fem. *bс╣Ыhatyai, so it is possible that bс╣Ыhat├й was introduced redactionally - but why?

Griffith

Flow for prosperity and constant Vigour, flow on for happiness and high perfection.
This is the wish of these friends assembled: this is my wish, O Soma Pavamana.

L├дutere dich gegen Raub und Totschlag, zum Wohlsein, zu hoher Vollkommenheit! Das w├╝nschen alle diese Freunde; das w├╝nsche ich, o Soma Pavamana.

Zum Wohlgedeihn zur Unversehrtheit riesle zum Heile und zu hoher Segensf├╝lle, Das w├╝nschen alle diese meine Freunde, das w├╝nsch’ auch ich, o Soma, hellentflammter!

Elizarenkova

тАЬThe Soma flows, the genitive rator of praises, the genitive rator of heaven, the genitive rator of the earth, the genitive rator of Agni, the genitive rator of the sun, the genitive rator of Indra, and the genitive rator of Viс╣гс╣Зu.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Soma purifies himselfтАФthe begetter of poetic thoughts, begetter of heaven, begetter of earth,
begetter of Agni, begetter of the sun, begetter of Indra, and begetter of Viс╣гс╣Зu.

Griffith

Father of holy hymns, Soma flows onward the Father of the earth, Father of heaven:
Father of Agni, Surya’s generator, the Father who begat Indra and Visnu.

Soma l├дutert sich, der Erzeuger der Gedanken, der Erzeuger des Himmels, der Erzeuger der Erde, der Erzeuger des Agni, der Erzeuger des Surya, der Erzeuger des Indra und der Erzeuger des Vishnu.

Grassmann

Es rieselt Soma, der Gebete Zeuger des Himmels Zeuger und der Erde Zeuger, Des Agni Zeuger und der Sonne Zeuger, des Indra Zeuger und der Zeuger Vischnu’s.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe Brahm─Б of the gods, the guide of the sages, the с╣Ыс╣гi of the pious, the buffalo of wild animals, the falcon of the vultures, the hatchet of deadly weapons, the Soma passes through the filter with a roar.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The Brahm─Б of the gods: i.e., the king of the gods; or, it may mean the br─Бhmaс╣Зa of the priests; the с╣Ыс╣гi: yaс╕е parokс╣гam pa┼Ыyati sa с╣Ыс╣гiс╕е, с╣Ыsirdar┼Ыan─Бt (Nirukta 2.11)

Jamison Brereton

Formulator for the gods, trail-blazer for the sage poets, seer for the inspired poets, buffalo of the wild beasts,
falcon of the birds of prey, axe of the treesтАФSoma goes rasping
through the filter.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Though the syntax is kept absolutely constant - nom. sg. + gen. pl. - there is a shifting functional relationship between the head noun and its genitive in the seven phrases here: the first two are roles Soma performs for the group identified by the gen., the next three a particular, and superior, individual token from the group (though the third pairing, тАЬseer for/of the inspired poets,тАЭ is ambiguous between the first type and the second), and the last is sort of a negative version of the role he plays for the group.

Griffith

Brahman of Gods, the Leader of the poets, Rsi of sages, Bull of savage creatures,
Falcon amid the vultures, Axe of forests, over the cleansing sieve goes Soma singing.

Geldner

Der Hohepriester der G├╢tter, der Pfadfinder der Seher, der Rishi unter den Beredten, der B├╝ffel unter den wilden Tieren, der Adler unter den Geiern, die Axt f├╝r die B├дume, geht Soma laut redend durch die Seihe.

Grassmann

Der G├╢tter Beter und der Priester F├╝hrer, der S├дnger Dichter und der Stier der Thiere, Der Geier Adler und die Axt der W├дlder, der Soma wandert singend durch die Seihe.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe purified Soma excites gratifying praises as a river (excites) the wave of sound; the showerer (of benefits) beholding the hidden (treasure) presides over these irresistible powers, knowing about the cattle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Like a river its wave, self-purifying Soma has sent the wave of speech pulsing forth, the hymns, the inspired thoughts.
Looking within, he surmounts these communities here below, a bull among the cows, recognizing them.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In p─Бda a, along with Geldner and Renou (see also OldenbergтАЩs comm. ad loc.) I read ┼лrm├нm twice, with both simile and frame; v─Бc├бс╕е so accented should be gen. sg., not acc. pl., and is therefore not parallel to the two acc. pls. in b, g├нraс╕е тАж man─лс╣г─Б╠Бс╕е.

The standard tr. interpr. the vс╣Ыj├бn─Б phrase as obj. of ant├бс╕е p├б┼Ыyan (e.g., Renou тАЬRegardant ├а lтАЩint├йrieur ces sectes (de fid├иles) prochesтАЭ). I instead take the part. in absolute usage (тАЬlooking withinтАЭ; cf. I.132.3) and construe the acc. with ─Б╠Бtiс╣гс╣нhati тАШ(sur)mountsтАЩ. This makes some spatial sense: if they are тАШbelowтАЩ (├бvar─Бс╣Зi) it is easy to mount them.

Renou and Ober (II.211) think that p─Бda d refers to copulation. Cf. esp. OberтАЩs тАЬDer Bulle besteigt die K├╝he, [die Kopulation] kennend.тАЭ Although тАЬmountтАЭ is a standard Engl. term for animal copulation, I am not at all sure that ─Б╠БтИЪsth─Б serves the same function, and I would esp. wonder about using the locative for the female participant(s). And I also doubt that it would need to be added that the bull knew how to do it!

Griffith

He, Soma Pavamana, like a river, hath stirred the wave of voice, our songs and praises.
Beholding these inferior powers in cattle, he rests among them as a Steer well-knowing.

Geldner

Er hat der Rede Welle hervorgewirbelt wie der Strom die Welle, er die Lobreden, die Gedanken, der Soma Pavamana, der diesen diesseitigen Opferverb├дnden ins Herz schaut, der Bulle steigt auf die K├╝he, sich auskennend.

Grassmann

Das Lied erregt er, wie der Strom die Welle, Ges├дnge Soma rieselnd und Gebete, Hinein auch schauend in die tiefsten Kl├╝fte, besteigt der Stier die K├╝he, der vertraute.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬ(Soma) who are the exhilarator, harming (the foe) in battles, (yourself) unharmed, who have a thousand streams, rush against the strength (of the enemy), Indu, who are being purified, the sage, uttering cries, urge on for Indra the wave of juice.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Exhilarating, vanquishing in battles but unvanquished,
thousand-spurtingтАФrush to the prize.
Purifying yourself for Indra, o drop, as inspired thinker raise a wave from the plant, driving the cows.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes iс╣гaс╣Зy├бn in d to mean тАШdesiringтАЩ (тАЬnach den K├╝hen verlangendтАЭ) as in the sim. passage he cites, III.50.3. But this verb stem always means тАШdrive, sendтАЩ (see RenouтАЩs n. ad loc.) and is, one way or another, derived from iс╣гс╣З─Б╠Бti тАШimpels, sendsтАЩ.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although these two vss. belong to two different hymns within the larger structure of IX.96, it is notable that the a-p─Бdas of both end with a form -v─Бtaс╕е; it is not impossible that the hymn consisting of 9-12 was attached here because of this concatenation, esp. given that the etymological figure in 8a is repeated in 11c of the other hymn. But the -v─Бta-forms belong to two different roots: 8a (/11c) ├бv─Бta- to тИЪvan тАШwin, vanquishтАЩ and 9a dev├бv─Бta-to тИЪvani тАШlove, cherish, long forтАЩ. The root affiliation of ├бv─Бta- is assured by the etymological figure in which itтАЩs found, vanv├бnn ├бv─Бtaс╕е тАЬvanquishing but unvanquishedтАЭ (cf. also VI.16.20, 18.1, IX.89.7 as well as the two occurrences in this hymn, 8a and 11c). But тИЪvan is an aniс╣н root, and we might expect a ppl. *-vata-, which does not occur; -v─Бta- is only phonologically proper to the seс╣н root тИЪvani . Got┼Н (1st Kl. 283-84 with n. 656), fld. by EWA (s.v. VAN), suggests that ├бv─Бta- (and, per EWA, other apparent seс╣н forms of тИЪvan) are analogic to the synonymous, rhyming but seс╣н root тИЪsani (s─Бt├б-, etc.). I certainly think the parallel forms of тИЪsani may well have contributed, but I think itтАЩs a mistake to discount potential confusion and conflation of forms of тИЪvani and тИЪvan, esp. since under certain circumstances тАШlove, long forтАЩ and тАШwinтАЩ can shade into each other.

English translation:

тАЬThe plural asing delightful Soma approached by gods (proceeds) to the pitcher to exhilarate Indra; Indu the thousand-streamed and vigorous proceeds like a strong horse to battle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The dear Soma, sought by the gods, (goes) around in the tub, the enjoyable one for IndraтАЩs exhilaration.
The drop of a thousand streams, a hundred prizes, goes like a
prizewinning team to the concourses.

In addition to its echoing ├бv─Бta- in 8, dev├бv─Бte is reminiscent of dev├бt─Бte in 3a.

My тАЬfor IndraтАЩs exhilarationтАЭ is a somewhat loose rendering of the double dative ├нndr─Бya тАж m├бd─Бya тАЬfor Indra, for exhilaration.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although these two vss. belong to two different hymns within the larger structure of IX.96, it is notable that the a-p─Бdas of both end with a form -v─Бtaс╕е; it is not impossible that the hymn consisting of 9-12 was attached here because of this concatenation, esp. given that the etymological figure in 8a is repeated in 11c of the other hymn. But the -v─Бta-forms belong to two different roots: 8a (/11c) ├бv─Бta- to тИЪvan тАШwin, vanquishтАЩ and 9a dev├бv─Бta-to тИЪvani тАШlove, cherish, long forтАЩ. The root affiliation of ├бv─Бta- is assured by the etymological figure in which itтАЩs found, vanv├бnn ├бv─Бtaс╕е тАЬvanquishing but unvanquishedтАЭ (cf. also VI.16.20, 18.1, IX.89.7 as well as the two occurrences in this hymn, 8a and 11c). But тИЪvan is an aniс╣н root, and we might expect a ppl. *-vata-, which does not occur; -v─Бta- is only phonologically proper to the seс╣н root тИЪvani . Got┼Н (1st Kl. 283-84 with n. 656), fld. by EWA (s.v. VAN), suggests that ├бv─Бta- (and, per EWA, other apparent seс╣н forms of тИЪvan) are analogic to the synonymous, rhyming but seс╣н root тИЪsani (s─Бt├б-, etc.). I certainly think the parallel forms of тИЪsani may well have contributed, but I think itтАЩs a mistake to discount potential confusion and conflation of forms of тИЪvani and тИЪvan, esp. since under certain circumstances тАШlove, long forтАЩ and тАШwinтАЩ can shade into each other.

Dear, grateful to the Gods, on to the beaker moves Soma, sweet to Indra, to delight him.
With hundred powers, with thousand currents, Indu, like a strong car-horse, goes to the assembly.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe ancient (Soma) the finder of treasure as soon as genitive rated, cleansed in the waters milked on the stone, the defender against enemies, the sovereign of the world, purified for the sacrifice, shows (the worshipper) the right way.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The primordial one, finding goods (even) while being born, being groomed in the waters, being milked on the stone,
protecting from imprecations, the king of creation, he finds the way for the sacred formulation as he is being purified.

Griffith

Born in old time as finder-out of treasures, drained with the stone, decking himself in waters,
Warding off curses, King of all existence, he shall find way for prayer the while they cleanse him.

Geldner

Als allererster Sch├дtzefinder geboren, im Wasser geputzt, auf dem Stein gemolken, vor ├╝bler Nachrede sch├╝tzend, der K├╢nig der Welt m├╢ge gel├дutert f├╝r das Segenswort den rechten Weg ausfindig machen.

Grassmann

Geboren ist er als der erste Spender, vom Stein gepresst und in der Flut gereinigt, Der Fluchabwehrer und der Weltbeherrscher, verleihe strahlend dem Gebete Fortgang.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬSoma Pavam─Бna, by you our ancient and wise progenitors performed their religious rites; harming the foes (yourself) unharmed slay the r─Бkс╣гasas and be liberal in enriching us with male offspring and horses.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yourself unharmed: avataс╕е = tair, i.e. ┼Ыatrubhir abhigataс╕е

Jamison Brereton

Because with you, self-purifying Soma, our insightful forefathers performed their (ritual) acts,
open up the barriers, vanquishing but unvanquished; become a
benefactor to us with heroes and with horses.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Geldner (see n. 11c) and Ober (I.311 with n. 791) point out, the first hemistich depicts the Vala myth, with тАЬforefathersтАЭ (pit├бraс╕е) a reference to the Aс╣Еgirases - made clearer by a similar but more explicit passage in the next hymn, IX.97.39. This mythic episode - the forefathers opening the Vala cave with the help of soma - provides the model for the appeal in c, for Soma to open the paridh├н- (paridh─л╠Бm╠Рr ├бporс╣Зu): paridh├н- is used explicitly of the barriers of the Vala cave in I.52.5. But as Geldner suggests (n. 11c), the poet here is calling on Soma to open up the livestock pens and provide us with the animals therein.

Griffith

For our sage fathers, Soma Pavamana, of old performed, by thee, their sacred duties.
Fighting unvanquished, open the enclosures: enrich us with large gifts of steeds and heroes.

Geldner

Denn mit dir, o Soma, haben unsere weisen V├дter vormals ihre Taten getan, o Pavamana. Ein un├╝berwundener ├Ьberwinder ├╢ffne du die Schranken; sei gegen uns freigebig mit S├╢hnen und Rossen!

Grassmann

Denn unsre alten weisen V├дter thaten durch dich, o heller Soma, ihre Werke, Die Wehren brich unangefochten, siegreich, sei m├дchtig uns durch Helden und durch Rosse.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAs you did flow to Manu possessing food, slaying enemies, acquiring wealth, having oblations, so now flow bringing us riches; abide you in Indra; make manifest (your) weapons.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Even as you purified yourself for Manu, as conferrer of vitality, smiter of foes, finder of wide space, accompanied by oblations,
just so purify yourself now, conferring wealth. Stand side-by-side by Indra. Generate weapons.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As pointed out in the published introduction, this vs. is strongly marked as a hymnfinal vs., with complementary y├бth─Б тАШeven asтАЩ (ab) and ev─Б╠БтАШin just this wayтАЩ (cd) clauses, bringing this 4-versed hymn to a close. The matches between clauses are more expicit than in some such structures: the two finite verbs, impf. ├бpavath─Бс╕е and impv. pavasva, match exactly save for tense/mood, and the root noun cmpd. vayodh─Б╠Бс╕е of p─Бda a is recast as a syntagm dr├бviс╣Зaс╣Г d├бdh─Бnaс╕е in c with the same root тИЪdh─Б.

The final p─Бda consists of two brief clauses, both somewhat aberrant. The first contains an idiom I have not found elsewhere, s├бm тИЪsth─Б + LOC. My tr., тАЬstand sideby-side by Indra,тАЭ is meant to capture this slightly off expression. The second clause, тАЬbeget/generate weapons,тАЭ is syntactically fine but semantically odd.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first vs. of the new hymn (13a) begins p├бvasva (see also pavasva in 14a), just as the last vs. of the previous hymn ended with pavasva (12c). Again, this concatenation may have led to the attachment of 13-16 at this point. Of course, p├бvasva is hardly a rare form in this maс╣Зс╕Нala.

Griffith

As thou didst flow for Manu Life-bestowing, Foe-queller, Comforter, rich in oblations,
Even thus flow onward now conferring riches: combine with Indra, and bring forth thy weapons.

English translation:

тАЬSoma who have exhilarating juice, who are connected with the sacrifice, clothed with water flow upon the elevated fleece; alight upon the water-holding pitchers, you who are most exhilarating, intoxicating, the especial beverage of Indra.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first vs. of the new hymn (13a) begins p├бvasva (see also pavasva in 14a), just as the last vs. of the previous hymn ended with pavasva (12c). Again, this concatenation may have led to the attachment of 13-16 at this point. Of course, p├бvasva is hardly a rare form in this maс╣Зс╕Нala.

Settle in vessels that are full of fatness, as cheering and most gladdening drink for Indra.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Soma), who flows in a hundred streams, pour rain from the firmament, you who are the giver of hundredfold (wealth), the bestower of food at the banquet of the gods; desirous of (the mixture) combine with the waters in the pitchers and with the curds and milk, prolonging our life.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Desirous of the mixture: or, with a noise

Jamison Brereton

Having a hundred streams, purify yourself into the rain from heavenтАФ thousand-winning, seeking the prize in pursuit of the gods,
bellowing along with the rivers in the tub, along with the ruddy (cows), prolonging our lifetime.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The pavasva in this vs. is construed with an acc. phrase, vс╣Ыс╣гс╣н├нс╣Г div├бс╕е. Geldner treats it as if it were a straight transitive: тАЬL├дutere … den Regen … herab,тАЭ while Renou supplies a participle to govern the acc.: тАЬclarifie toi (nous donnant) la pluie.тАЭ It is possible that something like RenouтАЩs solution is correct: that we should supply the preverb ─Б╠Бto form the lexeme ─Б╠БтИЪp┼л тАШattract through purificationтАЩ (see comm. ad IX.7.8); on occasion (see, e.g., IX.13.4 and comm. ad loc.), ─Б╠Бis missing, but the passage seems to require it. However, here I suggest that something different is going on: it is not that we want Soma to bring rain through his purification, but to become, turn into rain. See IX.97.44, 108.10

Griffith

Pour, hundred-streamed, winner of thousands, mighty at the Gods’ banquet, Pour the rain of heaven,
While thou with rivers roarest in the beaker, and blent with milk prolongest our existence.

Geldner

L├дutere mit hundert Str├╢men den Regen vom Himmel herab, tausendgewinnend, nach dem Siegerpreis strebend bei der G├╢tterladung! Mit den Str├╢men in dem Kruge zusammenbr├╝llend, mit den K├╝hen, unsere Lebenszeit verl├дngernd.

Grassmann

Des Himmels Regen riesle hundertstr├╢mig, beim G├╢ttermahl erlabend tausendspendend, Vereint mit Str├╢men rauschend zu der Kufe, mit Milch vereint verl├дngernd unser Leben.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis Soma (is) purified with praises, like a strong horse he overthrows (his) foes; (he is purified) like the strong milk milked from the cow, (flocked to by all) like a broad road, (and guided by the praisers) like a well-trained horse of burden.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

This very Soma, being purified by poetic thoughts, like a prizewinning steed just outstrips hostilities.
Like the milk milked out of Aditi, it is invigorating, broad like a way, like a draft-horse easy to control.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I donтАЩt know what ├нd contributes in b, beyond inducing accent on the verb t├бrati.

The standard tr. (Geldner, Renou, Ober [I.232]) take тАЬ(the milk) of AditiтАЭ as the frame, with the simile limited to p├бyo n├б dugdh├бm, e.g., тАЬTel le lait trait, (le lait) dтАЩAditi est fort.тАЭ I find this puzzling because Aditi has little to do with soma and has no reason to figure here. (On the phrase тАЬin the lap of AditiтАЭ in IX, see comm. ad IX.89.1.) Instead I think that it is soma that is being compared to the milk milked from Aditi; in other words, Aditi belongs to the simile. Since she is the archetype of motherhood, the milk of Aditi would be esp. rich and nurturing - тАЬmotherтАЩs milkтАЭ; indeed this might be a reference to the beestings or тАЬfirst milkтАЭ (p─лy┼л╠Бс╣гa-), with which soma is often compared (see comm. ad IX.85.9).

Oldenberg, Geldner, and Renou all make more of the gender mismatch in the simile urv ├мva g─Бt├║с╕е than I think is justified. Since the target of the simile is milk (p├бyaс╕е), and milk is neuter, I see no problem with attributing the neut. ur├║ to its тАЬattractionтАЭ to the neut.

p├бyaс╕е, even though, given the position of n├б, the simile should rightly be тАЬlike a broad wayтАЭ rather than тАЬbroad like a way.тАЭ The masc. suy├бmaс╕е in the next simile may result from the more animate quality of the content of the simile itself, the draught-horse.

Griffith

Purified with our holy hymns, this Soma o’ertakes malignities like some strong charger,
Like fresh milk poured by Aditi, like passage in ample room, or like a docile car-horse.

Geldner

Dieser Soma, der unter Gebeten gel├дutert wird, entgeht wie ein siegreicher Renner den Feinden. Wie gemolkene Milch ist die Milch der Aditi rasch zur Hand, breit wie ein Weg, wie ein Zugro├Я lenksam.

Grassmann

Ja, dieser Soma, durch Gebet gereinigt, besiegt die Frevler wie ein schnelles Streitross, Gleichwie gemolkne frische Milch der Milchkuh, wie freie Bahn, wie leicht gelenktes Zugthier.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬWell-armed, purified by those who express you, send your concealed desirable form (into the pitchers); like a horse bring us food in our desire for food; divine Soma, bring us life, bring us cattle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Having good weapons, being purified by the pressers, rush to the dear hidden name (of the cows? of Indra?),
to the prize, like a team with desire for fame, to V─Бyu, to the cows, o god Soma.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The bahuvr─лhi sv-─Бyudh├б- тАШhaving good weaponsтАЩ echoes the odd command that ends the previous hymn in this structure, 12d jan├бy─Б╠Бyudh─Бni тАЬbeget weapons!тАЭ This echo may have contributed to the attachment of 13-16 at that point in the text.

SomaтАЩs goal in b, тАЬthe dear hidden nameтАЭ (g├║hyaс╣Г c─Б╠Бru n─Б╠Бma), has a surprisingly large number of possible referents. L├╝ders (526) suggests the sun, Geldner (n.

16b) amс╣Ы╠Бta- the drink of immortality. I would add SomaтАЩs own name (see IX.92.2, 4 and comm. thereon), or the cows on the basis of IX.87.3 ap─лcy├аm g├║hyaс╣Г n─Б╠Бma g├│n─Бm, or the gods, as in the immed. preceding hymn IX.95.2 dev─Б╠Бn─Бс╣Г g├║hy─Бni n─Б╠Бma, or Indra on the basis of IX.109.14 b├нbharti c─Б╠Бrv ├нndrasya n─Б╠Бma.

Griffith

Cleansed by the pressers, armed with noble weapons, stream to us the fair secret name thou bearest.
Pour booty, like a horse, for love of glory God, Soma, send us kine, and send us Vayu.

Geldner

Gutbewaffnet, von den Pressenden gel├дutert, flie├Яe deinem lieben Geheimnamen entgegen, dem Siegerpreis entgegen wie ein Rennpferd aus Ruhmbegierde, dem Vayu entgegen, den K├╝hen entgegen, o Gott Soma!

Grassmann

Gereinigt von den Pressern, sch├╢nbewaffnet lass str├╢men dein verborgnes, theures Wesen, Lauf wie ein Ross zum Kampfpreis ruhmbegierig, zu Vaju hin, o Gott, zur Milch, o Soma.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThey cleanse the charming infant (Soma) at his birth; the Maruts decorate the bearer (of boons) with their troop; bring wise with songs, wise with wisdom, Soma passes clamorous through the filter.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Wise with wisdom: there is a plural y on the word, kavi; separating g─лbhiс╕е from kaviс╕е, the explanation is: he passes through the filter with praise

Jamison Brereton

The colt just born, the delightful one they groom; the Maruts in a flock beautify the cart horse.
Though being a poet by virtue of his hymns, a poet by his poetry, Soma goes rasping across the filter.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I donтАЩt know what the Maruts are doing here.

In c I have rendered the nom. pres. part. s├бn concessively, in its usual value, but itтАЩs not exactly clear what the concession would be. Perhaps the contrast is between Soma as poet - so emphasized by kav├нс╕е тАж k─Б╠Бvyena kav├нс╕е – and the less than melodious sound indicated by the root тИЪribh тАШsquawk, raspтАЩ (see comm. ad VI.3.6, IX.66.9).

Jamison Brereton Notes

These two vss. outfit Soma with the lexicon of poetry, with 17c concentrating on kav├н- and 18a on с╣Ы╠Бс╣гi-, though with kav├н- returning in p─Бda b

Griffith

They deck him at his birth, the lovely Infant, the Maruts with their troop adorn the Car-horse.
By songs a Poet and a Sage by wisdom, Soma joes singing through the cleansing filter.

Geldner

Das neugeborene Kind, das begehrenswerte, machen sie sauber; die Marut mit ihrer Heerschar machen das Zugpferd sch├╢n. Ein Seher durch seine Reden, ein Seher an Sehergabe geht Soma laut redend ├╝ber die Seihe.

Grassmann

Das neugeborne sch├╢ne F├╝llen streicheln und schm├╝cken auf der Fahrt die Marutscharen; Der Seher geht mit Seherkraft mit Liedern, als Seher Soma singend durch die Seihe.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThinking as a с╣Ыс╣гi, acting as a с╣Ыс╣гi, gaining heaven, praised by thousands, the guide of the wise, the mighty Soma desiring to attain the third region (heaven), being praised adds lustre to the illustrious (Indra).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Having the mind of a seer, a maker of seers, gaining the sun, having a thousand devices, trail-blazer for poets,
a buffalo, seeking to gain the third domain, Soma, as rhythm
[/the anuс╣гс╣нubh meter], regulates the vir─Бj (meter) according to rule.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The published translation does not render the rel. y├бс╕е since the rel. cl. is entirely nominal. It is not clear how far it extends - perhaps the first hemistich, perhaps through p─Бda c, perhaps only the first p─Бda - since Soma is nominative both in the rel. cl. and in the main cl. The main cl. must constitute at least the last p─Бda because the finite verb r─Бjati is unaccented.

The phrase padav─л╠Бс╕е kav─лn─Б╠Бm is found also in 6a.

What the referent of the тАЬthird domainтАЭ (tс╣Ыt─л╠Бyaс╣Г dh─Б╠Бma) is is unclear. L├╝ders (273), not surprisingly, has precisely mapped the spatial geography and considers the third domain to be heaven (1 earth, 2 midspace, 3 heaven), with the fourth, in the next vs., the samudra-, which is higher than heaven. I think it more likely that these are ritual references, quite possibly to locations on the ritual ground that Soma traverses on his journey (see dh─Б╠Бm─Бni ─Б╠Бry─Б in IX.63.14 and comm. thereon). If тАЬgaining the sunтАЭ (svarс╣г─Б╠Бс╕е) refers to SomaтАЩs uniting with the milk mixture (assimilated to the sun because of its gleaming whiteness), then the third domain, which comes after, might be the vessels near the ritual fire. If the dh─Б╠Бman- are not spatial but temporal, this could be a ref. to the third pressing. Geldner (n. 18c) takes it as reference to the forms or phases of soma; Renou tr. тАШstructureтАЩ without further elaboration.

As generally noted by tr. (Geldner, Renou, also Scarlatta [72]), p─Бda d involves a play on the names of the Anuс╣гс╣нubh and Vir─Бj meters. The published translation fails to register the pun on vir─Б╠Бjam, well captured by Scarlatta тАЬSoma herrscht nach Art eines Grossk├╢nigs.тАЭ I would now substitute a fuller (if more awk.) tr.: тАЬSoma, as rhythm [/ the Anuс╣гс╣нubh meter], rules as wide-ruling one [/regulates the Vir─Бj (meter) according to rule].тАЭ This tr.

assumes that vir─Б╠Бjam represents not only the acc. sg. of the rt. noun cmpd. vir─Б╠Бj-, but also the nom. sg. pres. part. *vir─Б╠Бjan to the them. pres. r─Б╠Бjati. This seems preferable to trying to construe it as an acc. sg. in the sense тАШwide-rulingтАЩ, and the interchange of final nasals would be fairly trivial for a pun. Scarlatta. (72 n. 97) notes that the lexeme ├бnu тИЪr─Бj is used in II.43.1 also of regulating meters, there G─Бyatr─л and Triс╣гс╣нubh. The preverb ├бnu also has to be read with с╣гс╣н├║p, as a cmpd decomposed and flanking r─Бjati (├бnu r─Бjati с╣гс╣н├║p), for the meter name. The technical references to meters here may be the culmination of the kav├н- / с╣Ы╠Бс╣гi- theme of 17-18.

These two vss. outfit Soma with the lexicon of poetry, with 17c concentrating on kav├н- and 18a on с╣Ы╠Бс╣гi-, though with kav├н- returning in p─Бda b

Griffith

Light-winner, Rsi-mindcd, Rsi-maker, hymned in a thousand hymns, Leader of sages,
A Steer who strives to gain his third form, Soma is, like Viraj, resplendent as a Singer.

Der wie ein Rishi denkend, zum Rishi machend, das Sonnenlicht gewinnend, tausend Weisen kennend, der Seher Pfadfinder ist, der B├╝ffel, der seine dritte Form gewinnen m├╢chte, der Soma tut es an Pracht dem prangenden Herrscher gleich, der Lobs├дnger.

Grassmann

Der Dichtergeist, der Dichter schafft und Glanz gibt, der S├дnger F├╝hrer, tausend Weisen kennend, Der Stier hinstrebend nach der dritten St├дtte misst nach dem Dreimass ab sein Lied, der Soma.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSeated on the ladles, praiseworthy, competent, supporting, acquiring cattle, flowing, bearing arms, attending upon the firmament, the sender of the waters, the mighty (Soma) attends the fourth sphere.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

I.e. the region of the moon which is above that of the sun

Jamison Brereton

Sitting in the cups, the falcon, the bird spreading (his wings), the cow-finding drop, bearing weapons,
accompanying the wave of the waters, the buffalo declares the sea to be the fourth domain.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I follow Geldner in interpr. vibhс╣Ы╠Бtvan- as тАШspreading (wings)тАЩ, an interpr. that Oldenberg finds at least possible and that Renou accepts. It is noteworthy - though IтАЩm not sure where it gets us - that the Avestan Hom Ya┼бt in Y. 9.14 contains the phrase v─лb╟Эr╟Э╧Сuuaс╣Зt╟Эm ─Бxt┼лir─лm supposedly тАЬwith pauses and repeated four times,тАЭ describing the recitation of the Ahuna Vairiia prayer, with the equivalent of our vibhс╣Ы╠Бtvan- (/-vant-) and tur─л╠Бya-. But the contexts are so different that it is hard to know what, if anything, to make of it - though if thereтАЩs a covert reference to recitational styles here it would continue the technical poetic vocab. of 18d.

The stem govind├║- тАШcow-findingтАЩ is found only here in the RV and nowhere else in Skt. (though govinda- is of course quite common later). As Renou notes, it is a play on ├нndu- тАШdropтАЩ and is immed. doubled by the synonym draps├б-.

The weapons of 16a (and 12d) return here.

I follow L├╝ders (273) and Renou in taking samudr├бm in c as part of a double acc. phrase with vivakti in d: тАЬdeclares the sea to be the fourth domainтАЭ - rather than as taking it as a 2nd obj. with s├бcam─Бnaс╕е as Geldner does (тАЬтАж der Meerflut sich gesellendтАЭ).

Accepting L├╝dersтАЩs interpr. of the syntax does not, however, require accepting his view that this is the heavenly ocean, higher than heaven. Again, I think itтАЩs a ritual ref. - perhaps to the waters that accompany him in p─Бda c.

Griffith

Hawk seated in the bowls, Bird wide-extended, the Banner seeking kine and wielding weapons,
Following close the sea, the wave of waters, the great Bull tells his fourth form and declares it.

Geldner

In dem Camugef├д├Я sitzend wie ein Falke, der die Fl├╝gel ausbreitende Vogel, der die K├╝he findende Tropfen, Waffen tragend, der Wasserwoge, der Meerflut sich gesellend, verk├╝ndet der B├╝ffel seine vierte Form.

Grassmann

Der Adler eilend, in der Sch├╝ssel nistend, der Tropfen Milch erlangend, Waffen tragend, Der Wasser Flut geleitend nach dem Meere, besingt der B├╝ffel seine vierte St├дtte.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬCleaning his person n like a richly-decorated man, flowing to acquire riches like a rapid (horse), rushing to the receptacle like a bull to the herd, (Soma) crying repeatedly enters the plural nks.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Like a richy decorated man: maryo na ┼Ыubhraс╕е; the plural nks: the ladles; the soma has already been effused and filtered

Jamison Brereton

Like a resplendent young blood grooming his own body, like a steed running to gain the stakes,
charging around the cask like a bull around the herds, constantly roaring he has entered the two cups.

Jamison Brereton Notes

SomaтАЩs journey from the filter (vs. 17) and across the domains on the ritual ground (vss. 18-19) reaches its end when he enters the two cups, presumably ready for the gods to consume.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Again these two vss. belong to separate mini-hymns, but they are clearly concatenated: k├бnikradat тАЬconstantly roaringтАЭ in 20d is repeated in the same metrical position in 21b (and cf. kr├бndan in 22d), and 20d camv├▓r ─Б╠Бvive┼Ыa тАЬhe has entered the two cupsтАЭ is immediately echoed by 21c camv├▓r ─Б╠Бvi┼Ыa тАЬenter the two cupsтАЭ (and cf. 22b kal├б┼Ы─Бm╠Р─Б╠Бvive┼Ыa).

Griffith

Like a fair youth who decorates his body, a courser rushing to the gain of riches,
A steer to herds, so, flowing to the pitcher, he with a roar hath passed into the beakers.

Geldner

Wie ein sch├╢ner J├╝ngling seinen K├╢rper putzend, wie ein Rennpferd laufend, um die Preise zu gewinnen, die Kufe umkreisend wie ein Bulle die Herde, ist er br├╝llend in die beiden Camugef├д├Яe eingezogen.

Grassmann

Den K├╢rper schm├╝ckend wie ein sch├╢ner Br├дut’gam, und eilend wie ein Ross zur Preiserlangung, Zum Fass rings str├╢mend wie ein Bull zur Heerde, ist in die Schalen br├╝llend er gedrungen.

English translation:

тАЬFlow, Indu, purified by the venerable (priests), rush through the filter crying repeatedly, sporting enter the plural nks purified, let your exhilarating beverage exhilarate Indra.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Purify yourself, o drop, as self-purifying one, with your mighty powers. Constantly roaring, rush around the fleeces.
Playing, enter the two cups while being purified. Let your exhilarating sap exhilarate Indra. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

Again these two vss. belong to separate mini-hymns, but they are clearly concatenated: k├бnikradat тАЬconstantly roaringтАЭ in 20d is repeated in the same metrical position in 21b (and cf. kr├бndan in 22d), and 20d camv├▓r ─Б╠Бvive┼Ыa тАЬhe has entered the two cupsтАЭ is immediately echoed by 21c camv├▓r ─Б╠Бvi┼Ыa тАЬenter the two cupsтАЭ (and cf. 22b kal├б┼Ы─Бm╠Р─Б╠Бvive┼Ыa).

Griffith

Flow on with might as Pavamana, Indu flow loudly roaring through the fleecy filter.
Enter the beakers sporting, as they cleanse thee, and let thy gladdening juice make Indra joyful.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHis copious streams flow forth; blended with the milk and curds he enters the pitchers; uttering chants the skilful chanter (Soma) hasten invoking (the gods) towards (the cups) like (a libertine) to the wife of a friend.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

His lofty streams have been sent surging forth. Anointed with cows he has entered the tubs. Making a melody [/performing the s─Бman], devoted to a melody
[/the s─Бman], attentive to poetic inspiration, roaring he goes as if to a comradeтАЩs sister.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Given the play on names of meters in 18d, itтАЩs quite possible that s─Б╠Бman- is a technical term here.

Although eti has a goal in its p─Бda (at least in the simile) and should therefore be read as a lexical verb of motion, it may also be functioning as an auxiliary in a periphrasis kr├бndann eti тАЬkeeps roaring,тАЭ which would be an analytic expression functionally equivalent to the тАЬintensiveтАЭ (that is, iterative-repetitive) k├бnikradat in 20d, 21b.

Griffith

His streams have been effused in all their fulness, and he hath entered, balmed with milk, the goblets.
Singing his psalm, well-skilled in song, a Chanter, be comes as ’twere to his friend’s sister roaring.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬO Pavam─Бna, eulogized (by the worshippers), distilling (into the receptacles), destroying the enemies, you go like a gallant to his mistress; falling like a bird alighting on the trees the Soma when purified alights upon the pitchers.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Smiting aside the rivals, self-purifying one, you go like a swain to his beloved, the drop besung.
Sitting in the woods like a flying bird, Soma, being purified, has settled in the tubs.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The same double reading may apply to eс╣гi in p─Бda a, which has a goal (again in a simile), but also could be read with the part. apaghn├бn тАЬhe keeps smiting rivals.тАЭ ┼Ыakun├│ n├б p├бtv─Б тАЬlike a flying birdтАЭ seems closely modeled on 19a ┼Ыakun├│ vibhс╣Ы╠Бtv─Б тАЬa bird spreading (its wings). In itself the expression is a bit puzzling. If the bird is тАЬflyingтАЭ it should not already be тАЬsittingтАЭ (s─л╠Бdan), and it seems unlikely that p├бtvan- is meant to distinguish it (as тАШflightfulтАЩ) from a flightless bird like a dodo.

Griffith

Chasing our foes thou comest, Pavamana Indu, besting, as lover to his darling.
As a bird flies and settles in the forest, thus Soma settles, purified, in goblets.

Geldner

Du gehst, o Pavamana, die Feinde aus dem Felde schlagend, wie der Buhle zur Liebsten, der besungene Saft. In die Holzkufe sich setzend wie der fliegende Vogel auf den Baum, pflegt sich der gel├дuterte Soma in die Kr├╝ge zu setzen.

Grassmann

O flammender, du gehst den Feind verjagend, besungen, Indu, wie zur Braut der Buhle; Wie V├╢gel fliegend setzt er auf das Holz sich, gereinigt sitzet Soma in den Kufen.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThe lustres, Soma, of you when being purified, approach with abundant milk with copious streams like a woman (giving milk to her child); the green-tinted Soma, the desired of many, has been brought to the waters and cries repeatedly in the pitcher of the god-loving (worshippers).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

As you purify yourself, Soma, your beams come here like a maidenтАФ the good milkers giving good streams.
The fallow bay granting many favors, led hither into the waters, has
roared in the tub of those who seek the gods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

A last p─Бda-init. form of тИЪkrand, ├бcikradat in d.

Griffith

With full stream and abundant milk, O Soma, thy beams come, like a woman, as they cleanse thee.
He, gold-hued, rich in boons, brought to the waters, hath roared within the goblet of the pious.

Geldner

Deine, des Pavamana, Glanzlichter kommen, o Soma, wie eine junge Frau, wie leicht zu melkende K├╝he, die sch├╢ne Milchstrahlen geben. Der Falbe wird ins Wasser gegossen, der Vielbegehrte; er br├╝llte im Kruge der Gottverlangenden.

Grassmann

Wie Br├дute gehn, o Soma, deine Strahlen, des hell entflammten, reich an Milch und Str├╢men, Das Ross mit busch’gem Schweif gef├╝hrt ins Wasser hat laut gewiehert in dem Kelch der Frommen.

рдЖрд░реНрдпрдореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╕реЛрдо) рд╣реЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЛрддреНрдкрд╛рджрдХ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдордиреН ! (рдкрд╡рдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп, рддреЗ, рд░реБрдЪрдГ) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдкрд╛рд╡рдХрд╕реНрдп рддрд╡ рджреАрдкреНрддрдпрдГ (рд╕реБрджреБрдШрд╛рдГ) рдпрд╛рдГ рд╕рдореНрдпрдХреН рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдкрд░рд┐рдкреВрд░рдпрд┐рддреНрд░реНрдпрдГ (рд╕реБрдзрд╛рд░рд╛рдГ) рд╢реЛрднрдирдзрд╛рд░рд╛рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрд╛ рднрдХреНрддрдЬрдирд╛рдирднрд┐ (рдпреЛрд╖реЗрд╡, рдпрдиреНрддрд┐) рдЕрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░реЗрдордХрд░реНрддреНрд░реА рдорд╛рддреЗрд╡ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ (рд╣рд░рд┐рдГ) рджреБрдГрдЦрдирд╛рд╢рдХрдГ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ (рдЖрдиреАрддрдГ) рдЙрдкрд╛рд╕рд┐рддрдГ (рдЕрдкреНрд╕реБ, рдкреБрд░реБрд╡рд╛рд░рдГ) рдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрд┐рд░реВрдкрдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рдгреНрдбреЗ рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрд╡рд░рдгреАрдпрдГ рд╕ рдЪ (рджреЗрд╡рдпреВрдирд╛рдВ) рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╢рдХреНрддрд┐рдореН рдЗрдЪреНрдЫреВрдирд╛рдореБрдкрд╛рд╕рдХрд╛рдирд╛рдВ (рдХрд▓рд╢реЗ) рд╣реГрджрдпреЗ (рдЕрдЪрд┐рдХреНрд░рджрддреН) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджреИрд╡ рд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рдпрддреЗреереирекрее рдЗрддрд┐ рд╖рдгреНрдгрд╡рддрд┐рддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рджрд╢рдореЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧреНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее
